============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG17)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is
\[
0.768873878858443\;(-1+P/8.670374869520632)\;(1-P/14.33285523805181)\;P \;+\;0.768873878858443\;P^{1/3}.
\]
Expand the polynomial part: it is a cubic polynomial in \(P\) with **no constant term** and **no linear term**:
\[
A\left(-P + \Big(\tfrac1{8.6703}+\tfrac1{14.3329}\Big)P^2 - \tfrac1{(8.6703)(14.3329)}P^3\right)
\]
so GT has the form
\[
\text{GT}(P)=\alpha P^{1/3} + \beta P^2 + \gamma P^3 + \delta P,
\]
with \(\alpha=0.7688...\), \(\delta=-0.7688...\neq 0\), and \(\gamma\neq 0\). Also GT is **independent of \(t\)**.

So any matching candidate must be able (by parameter choice) to produce exactly: a \(P^{1/3}\) term + a cubic polynomial in \(P\) (including a \(P^3\) term), with no extra nonpolynomial pieces (logs, exp, abs, max, trig, tanh), and no \(t\)-dependence.

Now check candidates:

1. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^2 + c2 P + c3 + c4\max(0,-P+c5)+\text{sin/log}\). Can zero out max and sin parts (set \(c4=0,c6=0\)), and set \(c3=0\). But **no \(P^3\)** term available ⇒ cannot match.
2. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), plus \(P^{c2}e^{c4P}\) and \(P^{c5}\). To avoid nonpolynomial, must kill exp term (set \(c3=0\) or \(c4=0\) but \(c4=0\) leaves \(P^{c2}\) which is ok). Still **no \(P^{1/3}\)** unless choose one power to be \(1/3\), but then still **no \(P^3\)** unless another power is 3; possible with \(P^{c5}\) and \(P^{c2}\). However there is no way to also get the exact linear term while keeping only those powers? Actually linear term exists via \(P*c1\). But you would need three distinct powers: \(1/3, 2, 3\) plus \(1\). Candidate can supply at most: \(P^2\), \(P^1\), \(P^{c2}\), \(P^{c5}\) (two adjustable powers). That could cover \(1/3\) and \(3\). So structurally it *could* match **if** we can remove any constant term (set \(c7=0\)) and remove exp (set \(c4=0\)). Then candidate becomes \(c0P^2+c1P+c3P^{c2}+c6P^{c5}\). Yes, that can represent \(P^{1/3},P,P^2,P^3\). But note: the \(P^2\) coefficient in GT is fixed and the \(P^2\) coefficient here is \(c0\) (free), fine. So **Candidate 2 can match** by setting \(c2=1/3\), \(c3=\alpha\); \(c5=3\), \(c6=\gamma\); \(c0=\beta\); \(c1=\delta\); \(c4=0\); \(c7=0\). ⇒ MATCH possible.
3. \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P\), plus rational \(P*c3/(Pc4+1)\), constant, max. To avoid nonpolynomial, set \(c6=0\), and rational term must be removed (set \(c3=0\)) or it introduces non-polynomial. Then no \(P^3\) ⇒ cannot.
4. Same as 3 but with tanh(t). Must remove tanh by setting \(c5=0\). Still no \(P^3\) ⇒ cannot.
5. Has \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), rational \(P^2*c2/(Pc3+1)\), \(P\), constant, max. Remove max. Rational term cannot become a pure \(P^3\) polynomial for all \(P\) (it’s not a polynomial unless \(c2=0\) or \(c3=0\), which yields \(P^2\) again). No \(P^3\) ⇒ cannot.
6. Depends on \(t\) and has \(e^{|P|}\). To match GT must be \(t\)-independent and no exp/abs; only possible by setting those coefficients to 0, leaving linear in \(P\) only ⇒ cannot.
7. Has \(P\exp(c2P)\) and \(t\)-term. Kill exp and t-term ⇒ only linear \(P\) terms ⇒ cannot.
8. Has \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P e^{c3P}\), and linear terms. Kill exp ⇒ no \(P^3\) ⇒ cannot.
9. Has logs, abs powers, and \(t^{c7}\). To match GT must kill those, leaving at best linear+constant ⇒ cannot.
10. Has \(P^{1/3}\) and polynomial up to \(P^3\) (explicit \(P^3*c1\), \(P^2\) terms, \(P\) terms) plus tanh(t). Set tanh coefficient \(c7=0\). Then we can set \(c1=\gamma\), combine \(P^2\) coefficients \(c2+c3+c4=\beta\), combine \(P\) coefficients \(c5+c6=\delta\), and set \(c0=\alpha\). No constant term present. ⇒ MATCH possible.
11. Has \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), linear terms, plus \(P\log(\cdot)\) terms. Must set those log coefficients \(c4=c6=0\). Then no \(P^3\) ⇒ cannot.
12. Only \(P^2\), \(P\), plus \(t^{c4}\) and constant ⇒ cannot.
13. Linear + sin(log) + constant ⇒ cannot.
14. Has \(t\)-dependence and \(P e^{c4P}\). Killing those leaves at most \(P^2,P\) ⇒ no \(P^3\) or \(P^{1/3}\) ⇒ cannot.
15. Has log term, two power terms \(P^{c2},P^{c4}\), and \(t^{c7}\). Kill log and t ⇒ can represent at most two powers plus maybe none linear unless one exponent is 1. But GT needs four powers \(1/3,1,2,3\). Only two adjustable power terms and no fixed \(P^2\) term. Cannot cover all required powers simultaneously ⇒ cannot.
16. \(P^2\) plus two \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\) terms and constant. Kill exp terms ⇒ no \(P^3\), no \(P^{1/3}\) ⇒ cannot.
17. Has \(P^2\), \(P\), exp-power term, max, constant. Kill exp and max ⇒ no \(P^3\), no \(P^{1/3}\) ⇒ cannot.
18. Has logs and tanh(t). Kill tanh and logs ⇒ only \(P^2,P\) ⇒ cannot.
19. Has rational \(P*c2/(Pc3+1)\) and a \(t\)-dependent factor. Kill \(t\)-term ⇒ still no \(P^{1/3}\) or \(P^3\) ⇒ cannot.
20. Has \(P^3\), \(P^2\) (several), \(P\), plus one power term \(P^{c5}\), constant. Set \(c5=1/3\) and \(c6=\alpha\), set \(c0=\gamma\), combine \(P^2\) coefficients to \(\beta\), set \(c4=\delta\), set constant \(c7=0\). ⇒ MATCH possible.
